Two things that were on KTLA (Los Angeles) the day of her death.    At 93, she was asked "Ms White, is there anything in the business you regret you never did?" The second was from a fan placing flowers on her star on the Walk of Fame: "All you ever needed to fall in love with Betty White was a television and a heart.". Betty White's death triggers all kinds of memories. One of the craziest happened when I transferred to BYU back in 1962. Several people had told me I looked a lot like Betty White. I didn't think much of it, but when a 3rd guy told me that again, I made up a totally fictitious story, that I was her daughter, but the family didn't want any publicity about me going to BYU.      That tall tale went on for several days, until I had to tell him the truth! He was so upset, and mad at me for tricking him!! To repent of my deceit, I ended up ironing all his shirts for my self-applied penance! (Back in the days when everything had to be ironed!!      So, Betty White, a fond adieu. You've entertained us so well, for so long....and may my deceitful past (with this confession) be laid to rest as well!

She paid for a private plane to relocate otters and penguins from Audubon Aquarium of the Americas in New Orleans in the aftermath of 2005â€²s Hurricane Katrina. Unselfish, caring, empathetic, strong willed who championed causes near and dear to her heart. Who doesn't everbody love Betty White?   Betty was a Unitarian, believing that we should, "affirm unconditional, universal love as a foundation and grounding for our actions in the world."  Unitarians believe in God, but reject the idea of eternal punishment.  My mother, who was likewise Unitarian, reminds me of Betty White (or is it the other way around?).  Both women believed that people who do evil things become their own punishment.          Yet, does that really work?  For example, I am not sure why, but I am still absolutely devastated over the death of young girl, Polly Klaas, some 30 years ago - yet, I have only seen her picture.  She was kidnapped out her own bedroom, brutally mistreated, then murdered.  The killer, Richard Allen Davis, laughed at her trial, at the suffering of her dear, poor parents - heart-breaking is not the word!  Yet, should such great evil go unpunished?  Is that true justice?          It is written that, one day soon, Jesus Christ will judge the world in righteousness.  Just as my anger has been greatly kindled by Davis, so God's anger is good and right; all injustice will be punished.  For those who disagree, do you believe the Richard Allen Davis should not be punished?  For example, should he have life in a paradise resort?  Such thinking is almost as vile as his dispicable act!             Yet, God will not just punish those who destroy families, but it is written that all liars will have their place in the lake of fire.  Heaven is totally just; we are not.  Jesus Christ died on a cross as punishment for the sins of the world - even for sweet, charming ladies like Betty!  I hope that she put her trust in Christ, that she was made new - born again - by the blood Christ!  I hope that everyone will!          Jesus Christ is the light of the world.

The Golden Girls were sorta an accidental replacement for my atrocious biological mother. I remember it being offered as an option for something to watch when I was in the hospital at about 5 years old, and at the time...I thought it was gonna be a superhero cartoon. I was half right, those legendary women helped develop the man I am today, I know that sounds ridiculous but when it is a choice between abusive drug addict or 4 nutty older ladies who, as it turns out were just as wonderful in real life. The choice was easy. So, when Betty White left us, the world got a little colder and darker for me. If it had that impact on me, I can only imagine the impact this had on those who were a part of her everyday life. For these reasons, I mourn the death of fun.  On the upside, she probably got the last laugh. And if anyone could plan and deliver a joke like this, it would be her. So, instead of letting it keep me down, I am gonna go on doing what she spent her whole life putting out in the world. Positivity, smiles and laughter!  We will miss you, Betty. Thank you for making this world bearable!

You missed one of the funniest appearances on St. Elsewhere that proves Betty and her iconic character Sueanne Nivies (Mary Tyler Moore Show) have become part of our cultural lexicon.  Betty had a supporting role as a doctor on the hit show St. Elsewhere.  In here first appearance in the series, in one scene where she has joined the hospital team, she is walking with other doctors down a corridor, discussing a medical procedure when a man at the end of the corridor sees the group of doctors; the man runs up to the group grabs Betty White's hand and excitedly says, Sueanne....Sueanne Nivins.  To which Betty says, "No, I am sorry, you must have me confused with someone else."  The man insists, "No, I am sure, you are Sueanne Nivins, the Happy Home-maker."  Two orderlies run up to the man and forcibly escort the man away, all they while with him yelling, It's Sueanne Nivins, the Happy Home-maker!"   One of the other doctors in the group says to Betty, "Oh, I am sorry doctor, that is one of our mental patience who excaped from the other wind."    The only reason the writers of that show could get away with such a direct reference to a character in another show and it make any sense was if the character of Sueanne Nivins the Happy Home-maker was universally known and more importantly, loved by the public -- a testament to how Betty imbued the character with like-ability.

#15 - I'm sorry, but this one makes no sense. One thing that the racist South back then definitely had no problems with.... was a Black entertainer singing and dancing. A number of Black entertainers traveled through the night club circuit back then.   No, they couldn't eat there, they couldn't get a drink there. They wouldn't be booked unless the owner of the travelling show was White. But again, Southern audiences back then had zero issues with Black entertainers showing up to sing and dance for them.   An elderly neighbor of mine used to do the Southern circuit. In many places, Jim Crow laws placed a curfew on how late Black citizens could be outside. As night club entertainment, he told me it was not uncommon for such entertainers to be stopped by the local police on the way back to their hotels after a show was over.   He told me how he would carry a business card with his boss's telephone number. The entertainer would get put in jail, then the number on the card was called to verify his identity. His boss would tell the sheriff that he was one of his. Then offer free tickets to the next show for the sheriff and his wife if the entertainer was driven back to his hotel room safely.  That's just how it was done back then. So, I'm sorry but #15 makes no sense.

Betty White wasn't just a nice lady.  People know about her work for humane treatment of animals, but maybe because it was back in the 1950s and 60s, we've forgotten what a trailblazer she was.  Her production company was female led.  Bandy Productions produced her first TV show "Life with Elizabeth" when she was only 28.  And she riled up controversy by casting Arthur Duncan, a black man, as a regular cast member on "The Betty White Show," telling critics who disagreed with the decision to "...just live with it "  She was also a supporter of the LGBTAQ+ community even back in the 70s.  We were lucky to have her.  I'm so glad that Ms MOJO recognized all this.
Rest in peace Betty. Glad to know that you died painlessly and peacefully, and what type of year 2022 is going to be. We will always love and remember you. Your spirit lives on.

There's an episode of Golden Girls where Betty White's character says something I'll never forget and I found it to be pretty prophetic and ironic. They (the girls) have to put a dear friend, who had no other family or friends, into a nursing home and they had to fight for her rights to get proper care. Anyways in that episode, the girls Rose, Blanche, Dorothy, and Sophia, are talking about how they'll stay friends forever and even go to the same nursing home if they have to. Then Betty White's character states, "what happens when there's only one of us left?" And low and behold, Rose, Betty White's character WAS the last one left out of all 4 of the characters/actresses. I always found that to be really weird, idk why.  I'm so saddened by the loss of such an amazing woman. I know that I didn't know her personally, but from what I understand of her and her character, she's someone I definitely look up to. Her love of animals, for one, and the fact that she never remarried after the love of her life, a game show host by last name of Lundron, (I think that's what it is) passed away in 1981. She said she just knew she would never feel the same towards any other man. She's a legend in her own right and I really wished she'd made it to her 100th birthday. When I was about 5 years old, I appeared on the Al Jarvis TV show in Los Angeles where Betty White was the sidekick. It was a live show, and she also did the commercials. I was picked out of the audience to eat a piece of Langendorf Bread on cue but at the moment she told the camera "Everyone Loves Langendorf Bread!" and the camera turned to me, I refused. My mom had always told me not to take things from strangers and so I said no. After a few seconds of trying to coax me, she finally gave up and turned to the camera to say, "Well ALMOST everyone loves Langendorf Bread."  About a dozen years ago, I write her a letter reminding her of the incident long ago and to my surprise she wrote back, saying she remembered the moment, and reminding me "it was okay now to eat my Langendorf Bread!" I don't know if she really remembered or was just being polite, but I had her note framed and gave it to my mom for her birthday a few years before she died. It was one of my mom's treasured memories.  RIP, Betty!  I will eat a sandwich i your honor tonight.
